The tower consists of over 18,000 iron pieces and features four massive, open-latticed piers that converge at the second level. As this design ascends, it carves out a unique and gradual taper in its wake. Two charming observation decks, often overlooked by visitors, can be found near the base. Since its completion in 1889, the Eiffel Tower has been coated in a uniform brownish-grey hue, securing its status as one of the world's most recognized landmarks.

From its base, the tower ascends skyward, each level unveiling an intricate tapestry of ornate detail. Two hidden gems, often overlooked by tourists, lie beneath this grand structure, offering stunning panoramic vistas to the fortunate few. From its inception in 1889, the Eiffel Tower has commanded global attention, radiating an enduring allure of grandeur, and securing a coveted place among the pantheon of historical landmarks that have captivated the collective human imagination. Shrouded by twilight, where the sun bids farewell and stars make their appearance, the esteemed silhouette of the ancient tower stands firm, an enigma that defies time's relentless march.
